    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer3301420616436859447"><b><i>The Breakfast Club</i> meets <i>Pretty Little Liars</i>, <i>One of Us Is Lying</i> is the story of what happens when five strangers walk into detention and only four walk out alive. Everyone is a suspect, and everyone has something to hide.</b> <br/><br/>Pay close attention and you might solve this.<br/><br/>On Monday afternoon, five students at Bayview High walk into detention.<br/> Bronwyn, <b>the brain, </b> is Yale-bound </span>
  <span id="freeText3301420616436859447" style="display:none"><b><i>The Breakfast Club</i> meets <i>Pretty Little Liars</i>, <i>One of Us Is Lying</i> is the story of what happens when five strangers walk into detention and only four walk out alive. Everyone is a suspect, and everyone has something to hide.</b> <br /><br />Pay close attention and you might solve this.<br /><br />On Monday afternoon, five students at Bayview High walk into detention.<br /> Bronwyn, <b>the brain, </b> is Yale-bound and never breaks a rule. <br /> Addy, <b> the beauty, </b> is the picture-perfect homecoming princess. <br /> Nate, <b>the criminal</b>, is already on probation for dealing.<br /> Cooper, <b>the athlete</b>, is the all-star baseball pitcher.<br /> And<b> </b>Simon, <b> the outcast</b>, is the creator of Bayview High's notorious gossip app.<br /><br />Only, Simon never makes it out of that classroom. Before the end of detention, Simon's dead. And according to investigators, his death wasn't an accident. On Monday, he died. But on Tuesday, he'd planned to post juicy reveals about all four of his high-profile classmates, which makes all four of them suspects in his murder. Or are they the perfect patsies for a killer who's still on the loose? <br />Everyone has secrets, right? What really matters is how far you would go to protect them.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Hannah, yes, that was the original inspiration -- The Breakfast Club with a criminal twist. I've always been interested in the concept of different<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Hannah, yes, that was the original inspiration -- The Breakfast Club with a criminal twist. I've always been interested in the concept of different types of people being brought together and having to interact with one another, and thought that adding a mystery would raise the stakes in an interesting way.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_more_filters_span_tip_681').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_1794065627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1794065627" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1794065627?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      Solomon ✴ The Bookish King
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=suspenseful-clues-and-thrilling-rev">suspenseful-clues-and-thrilling-rev</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1794065627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5725618374935292848">What a marvelous, delectable read! There was something so addictive about this book; it felt at times distinctly young adult while also having moments that felt so well done it was beyond the stereotype of what a teenage thriller tends to be. It’s taken me 4 days just to collect my thoughts to the point that I can attempt writing a proper review, and I’m certain this will be one of the most talked about books in the YA genre this Spring/Summer season. My issues with this book were minor, and I’l</span>
  <span id="freeText5725618374935292848" style="display:none">What a marvelous, delectable read! There was something so addictive about this book; it felt at times distinctly young adult while also having moments that felt so well done it was beyond the stereotype of what a teenage thriller tends to be. It’s taken me 4 days just to collect my thoughts to the point that I can attempt writing a proper review, and I’m certain this will be one of the most talked about books in the YA genre this Spring/Summer season. My issues with this book were minor, and I’ll get to those later, but when I first picked up this book I knew I would enjoy it based on the description stating “Breakfast Club meets Pretty Little Liars”, two things I love to pieces. While this was in some ways a traditional whodunnit, I believe many of the minor influences were the reason this novel reads so well.<br /><br />According the the books I’ve logged on Goodreads, I’ve managed to read over 700 mystery, thriller, and suspense novels. That is an overwhelming number of books that tend to be fiercely judged on their ability to provide a solid, mind-blowing twist. The reason I mention this is due to the fact that it is very difficult for me to pick up a mystery and not have it solved in the first 10% if the clues are provided; otherwise, I typically pick it up when said character is first introduced into the narrative. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395.One_of_Us_Is_Lying" title="One of Us Is Lying by Karen M. McManus" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us Is Lying</a> is bound to be one of many fabulous novels that gets thrown into that category and is scrutinized solely by it’s ability to keep the reader guessing “whodunnit” until the big reveal. Again, I mention this because I think it would be a grave mistake for the reader to be so focused on this aspect when the book has so much more to offer! Personally, I had it figured out in the first chapter. As stated in the summary, the pieces are there for the reader to put together if they are clever enough. I applaud the author for her cleverness and storytelling abilities; there will be many readers who will be fooled by the red herrings and receive that glorious <b>
  <i>AHA</i>
</b> moment at the big reveal. Why am I rambling on about this you ask? I really want to drive home the point of what makes this book stand out from others that are similar.<br /><br /><b>The Characters.</b> It is a rare day indeed that I find fleshed out, grounded, relatable characters that draw me in to a young adult narrative the way that these did here. My <b>
  <i>AHA</i>
</b> moment may not have come during the big twist, but it certainly came in waves abounding throughout my experience journeying with these various high school kids. I was sure this would be another read with those stereotypical teenagers that give contemporary YA novels a bad rep; for crying out loud the stereotypes are printed on the inside of the book cover in the description! I think this was a clever move by the publisher and author; if other readers pull the same underestimation as I did, they will be more than pleasantly surprised at what they get out of this book. In referral to the wrapping up of characters and not the twist, the ending was one of the best I’ve seen in awhile. There is no gag worthy happily ever after where everyone is perfectly paired up in couples and they ride off into the sunset on their baby unicorns while the sun beats down on their pimple free faces…. No, while there are some upbeats moments, the ending is messy and real and I welcomed it whole heartedly. People made mistakes beyond the central narrative and there were consequences and some things were left open-ended in the way that makes you wonder what their eventual decisions lead to. I’m extremely pleased that the author chose to take some risky leeway with her writing direction and applaud her with a standing ovation.<br /><br />Alright, I said I would get to the minor issues and I kind of lied. Please don’t hate me, but there was a tiny aspect of this book that I thought I could get past, and even though I can’t discuss it outright (because these spoilers involve blowing the entire plot of the book), my conscience just wouldn’t let me finish this review without mentioning them in the broadest of terms. Again, I applaud the author for tackling some really tough issues and concerns in this book, and I don’t think she wrote anything wrong on her end. I think it’s more of an issue I’ve seen present itself across a wide number of YA books recently. Some who may be dealing with mental illness may perceive the outcome of this novel in an unrealistic way and I can see the possibility of various readers being split on their opinions of some of the content presented. I will say, I feel it was handled better in this book than in others I have read previously. As always, if you’ve read this book early or once you have a chance to read it and would like to discuss, please feel free to private message me and I’ll gladly have a respectful chat with you.<br /><br />This is a review I’ve been struggling to write for a few days now and I hope I’ve done it justice. There just aren’t words to describe how completely readable this book really is. McManus did such a fabulous job of making me just as interested in the individual secrets and side stories of the “Murder Club” as I was in the central mystery surrounding Simon’s death. The author had me convinced that this couldn’t possibly be her debut novel, and if this is what she has published first, I can only imagine the treats we will receive in written form from her down the road. I’m a committed fan now and I can’t wait to see what she publishes next. Highly recommended to teens, sure, but I think loads of adults are going to enjoy this one as well. There’s something really special and unique to this story that defies the boundaries of age gaps and will have me remembering it for months to come.<br /><br /><b>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my copy; it was a pleasure to post my honest thoughts here. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5725618374935292848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2019039414" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2019039414" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2019039414?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2019039414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5306069124747804065">I'd give this 4.5 stars.<br/><br/>If <b>
  <i>One of Us Is Lying</i>
</b> was a television series, I would binge-watch it wholeheartedly. It's been a while since I've gotten so into a book I've devoured the majority of it in one sitting when I haven't been on a plane. This hooked me completely, and I'm surprised how much I liked it.<br/><br/>Five students have detention one afternoon. There's Cooper, the golden boy and star baseball player trying to decide between college and the major leagues; Bronwyn, the class valedictorian w</span>
  <span id="freeText5306069124747804065" style="display:none">I'd give this 4.5 stars.<br /><br />If <b>
  <i>One of Us Is Lying</i>
</b> was a television series, I would binge-watch it wholeheartedly. It's been a while since I've gotten so into a book I've devoured the majority of it in one sitting when I haven't been on a plane. This hooked me completely, and I'm surprised how much I liked it.<br /><br />Five students have detention one afternoon. There's Cooper, the golden boy and star baseball player trying to decide between college and the major leagues; Bronwyn, the class valedictorian who plans to follow her family's legacy and go to Yale; Addy, one-half of the picture-perfect couple and a homecoming princess; Nate, the bad boy, on probation for dealing drugs (and still selling them not so secretly); and Simon, the despised (and kind-of feared) creator of About That, Bayview High's gossip blog. They're all in detention for something none of them did, and they can't understand why the teacher doesn't believe them.<br /><br />Before detention is over for the day, Simon is dead, and apparently, it wasn't an accident. It's not long before investigators discover that the next day, Simon was planning to publish items about Cooper, Bronwyn, Addy, and Nate—items which could potentially destroy all of their lives. Suddenly the four of them are the suspects in Simon's murder, and are pariahs among their fellow students, most of whom hated Simon until he died, then turned him into a tragic figure.<br /><br />Suddenly four people who weren't really friends (or at least since childhood) are brought together. Each claims their innocence—but is one of them lying, or did someone else get involved? And how, when it was just five of them in the classroom that day? Can they clear their names and get their lives back?<br /><br />It turns out that Bronwyn, Cooper, Addy, and Nate all have secrets they'd prefer to have kept hidden. In some cases these aren't even the secrets that Simon threatened to expose. But when the truth is revealed it will impact their relationships with each other and their friends, as well as their futures. Can they handle it?<br /><br />Karen McManus did a great job with this book. It's amazing—she basically took most of the typical high school stereotypes, yet gave her characters a little more depth than you'd expect. Even though you probably will have suspicions of how the plot will unfold (and most of those suspicions will be correct), it's still interesting the way McManus pulls everything together. I couldn't get enough of this book, and even though the story wrapped up, I wouldn't have minded if it ran longer.<br /><br />This was a great read. And let's put it this way: only for a novel as skillfully written as <b>
  <i>One of Us Is Lying</i>
</b> would make me willing to relive memories of some of the angst, emotions, drama, and insecurities of high school. (And since you know so many books have me singing a particular song, for no reason whatsoever, this book had me singing "One of Us" by ABBA. But this was an easy one: the song actually has the lyric "One of us is lying.")<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5306069124747804065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027451933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10650217458311935668"><br/>Hi hello I’m coming at you live from the bog of eternal satisfaction on this warm wednesday night in July because <b>THIS BOOK.</b><br/><br/>I finished this book with the biggest cheesiest grin on my face, I don’t even know what plane of existence that was but there were a lot of corny feelings involved (any planets I can blame that on??). It’s like I was floating on a cloud or something. I was overwhelmed with so many emotions for no reason and I guess my cotton candy heart just went off!!! I wish at least it w</span>
  <span id="freeText10650217458311935668" style="display:none"><br>Hi hello I’m coming at you live from the bog of eternal satisfaction on this warm wednesday night in July because <b>THIS BOOK.</b><br><br>I finished this book with the biggest cheesiest grin on my face, I don’t even know what plane of existence that was but there were a lot of corny feelings involved (any planets I can blame that on??). It’s like I was floating on a cloud or something. I was overwhelmed with so many emotions for no reason and I guess my cotton candy heart just went off!!! I wish at least it was raining so at least I could go stand in it for the drama!!<br><br>Ok seriously. I need $$ not feelings *squashes my emotions with my bare hands* <br><br>So as I was saying, this book was just <b>so good, so cinematically, tangibly exciting, so FULFILLING TO THE CORE</b> and I’m willing to bet that if someone threw it off a cliff, I'd probably dive after it tbh!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498686503i/23152285.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s a universal truth that I am actually and unambiguously and inappropriately obsessively 100% full scale high key addicted to reading crime books and watching crime documentaries and having in-depth knowledge of incriminating shit. My aesthetics would just be capsule hotels and forever I can just chill in a padded bubble and read thrillers or watch crime shows<br><br>Which is why I was so excited for this book and boy, <b>it did not disappoint</b>!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>what is this book about?</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Basically that after reading it, I’ve decided that I’m living my life until someone frames me for murder, which won’t be so hard to achieve since I spend so much of my time alone that if I was ever falsely accused for a crime I would literally never have an alibi. Besides, I wonder how long before a person’s viewing history and library receipts can be used against them in court like, “the defendant has stacks of crime books and had viewed 46 straight hours of crime shows before the murder occurred… sketchy, your honor. sketchy.”<br><br>I’m actually just kidding. Please if you’re connected to me in any way, never commit any crime I don’t think I can deal with the stress of a police interview and if I get falsely accused, I will probably just fucking start bawling!!<br><br>Anyway, back to the book.<br><br>I honestly don’t know what the hell to tell y’all that won't be spoilery, so just know that I can't wait to have kids so I can make them read this book and realise the repercussions of getting detention (<b>i.e being framed for murder</b>.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498686503i/23152286.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>honestly though, <b>this book was just so?? fun??</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“She's a princess and you're a jock," he says. He thrusts his chin toward Bronwyn, then at Nate. "And you're a brain. And you're a criminal. You're all walking teen-movie stereotypes.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The characters seemed like puppets attached to a string, as if the entire plot was just this girl playing on her phone and they’re all her neko atsume cats dying because she got bored of the app.<br><br><b>And so?? angsty??</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“These murder club meetings are becoming a regular thing. We need a new name, though.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I existed as both a teenager and a wealthy 18th century middle aged woman who needs to lie down for hours after anything remotely distressing happens while reading this. Really. I had one foot in a psychiatric breakdown and the other one in unattractive slippers trying to solve this.<br><br>But <b>I TOTALLY GUESSED IT</b> and I think it’s due to the fact that I'm morbid and too angsty and I am always aware of all of the worst worse things that could possibly happen at any given time. It’s like constantly being held hostage by hypothetical situations.....ok jesus fine don't look at me like that, I guessed it by the end but listen, I would've guessed it earlier if I wasn't busy obsessing over a CERTAIN OTP!!!!)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>The characters:</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I think my biggest shift in perspective has been going from “can I pay the universe a bribe to never send me any of these characters as real life people” to being like “wow I’d take care of you and care about you so hard!!” So that just goes to show you what a spectacular character development they’ve undergone. I literally love them so much and it might seem like my whole life currently revolves around them but yes it does!!<br><br>Also did I mention that <b>Nate</b> is my favorite?? bc he is, I mean he's the kind of guy you date to disappoint your parents but if someone is willing to throw stones at their girlfriend’s window so she can climb down the conveniently placed tree and go make out in a car, you bet they're my fav.<br><br>Okay, that’s it for my Ted talk thank you for listening goodbye and goodnight!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10650217458311935668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1884772778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1884772778" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884772778?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781524714680" href="/book/show/32682118-one-of-us-is-lying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884772778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11252505431133051494"><b>Content warning:</b> Harmful representation of sexuality and mental illness.<br/><br/>This book was such a disappointment because I was REALLY enjoying it up until the last 3rd or so. I seriously thought this would be a 4 or 5 star read. However, upon finishing, I strongly believe that this book should not have been published as is. It's ignorant and damaging.<br/><br/>Aside from the parts that I found harmful, the writing was very trope heavy and relied on too many stereotypes for character development. I didn't think</span>
  <span id="freeText11252505431133051494" style="display:none"><b>Content warning:</b> Harmful representation of sexuality and mental illness.<br /><br />This book was such a disappointment because I was REALLY enjoying it up until the last 3rd or so. I seriously thought this would be a 4 or 5 star read. However, upon finishing, I strongly believe that this book should not have been published as is. It's ignorant and damaging.<br /><br />Aside from the parts that I found harmful, the writing was very trope heavy and relied on too many stereotypes for character development. I didn't think there was anything new here. The one thing I did like about the book is that McManus did build suspense well and kept me guessing. She casts suspicion on so many characters that you start questioning everything. This would have been a good mystery if it hadn't used people's identities for shock value. This is othering. These are some 90s plot twists that I'm honestly surprised flew by a publishing team in 2017.<br /><br />I'm going to talk about these things in depth under the spoiler tag below because I know everyone has a different threshold for what they consider to be spoilery. I personally don't think these things should be written as spoilers, but that's how this book treats them so it's how I'm treating this review.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><u>Sexuality</u><br />All the characters have secrets that come to light throughout the book and the first red flag for me was about 2/3 or so in when Cooper is revealed to be gay. This was written as if it should be scandalous and to try and shock the reader because there is a distinct moment earlier in the book where you are led to believe the person he's flirting with is a girl.<br /><br />Cooper's reasoning for wanting to stay closeted felt very realistic and might be relateable to some readers. It's not that his storyline has no value, I just think that sexuality shouldn't be used as a plot twist.<br /><br />Further harm is done when part of the plot includes Cooper being publicly outed against his will. This could definitely cause some anxiety for people who are closeted or have been forceably outed before. Be cautious.<br /><br />I am not gay and can't tell you how to feel about these things. I've heard from LGBTQIA+ readers who loved the depiction and others who hated it. When I hear many LGBTQIA+ reviewers I follow saying sexuality shouldn't be written as a plot twist and that storylines involving being outed can be triggering, these are the best guidelines I can go by with my reviews since I am not personally affected by it. You are allowed to feel however you feel about it. I'm just warning those who MAY be harmed by it that this is present.<br /><br /><u>Mental Illness</u><br />There are a couple of characters in the book that are said to be depressed and one of them was Simon, the boy who died. The final plot twist is that Simon wasn't murdered, but killed himself. Again, I think that some of Simon's feelings that surround his depression could be very relateable to teenagers, but I had three huge issues with how his suicide was portrayed.<br /><br />First, depression is villanized because Simon is portrayed as a terrorist. His main motivation was wanting the infamy of a school shooter. He wanted to cause the same amount of damage, but in a way he deemed better. Problem: Depression does not equal being a terrorist! Mental illness being portrayed as wrong and evil is such a tired depiction.<br /><br />Second, a side character was also said to be depressed and she was his accomplice. She framed his death on the other 4 students by planting evidence. Through her, depression is villainized once again.<br /><br />Third, STOP TREATING SUICIDE LIKE A MYSTERY TO BE SOLVED. It's a mental illness, not sensational entertainment!<br /><br />Depression is something I know personally and have watched family members deal with, and how this book handled it was like a stab in the gut. Is this really what the world thinks of me? Again, not saying you have to agree with my thoughts on it, but this hurt me and affected my enjoyment of the book. I just think these twists are so tired and perpetuate stigmas against LGBTQIA+ people and people with mental illness.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />For those who may be hurt by the mishandling of sexuality or mental illness, I would suggest being cautious of this book. If you're a reader who is oblivious to or unhurt by bad rep, you'll probably enjoy this book going by all the shining reviews it has.<br /><br />Other things of note:<br />-Bronwyn is biracial (white &amp; Colombian).<br />-Addy's POV is very shallow and portrays a terrible relationship and girl drama. (But she has a good growth arc.)<br />-The drug-dealing bad boy trope is heavy.<br />-The audiobook narrators were great at their jobs.<br />-If you loved the book, that's great. I didn't, and this was why.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11252505431133051494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer18298689304824719831">4 to 4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Every time I walk into the living room my wife is watching Pretty Little Liars or Revenge or Riverdale or Veronica Mars or . . . well, you get the idea. Sometimes I watch a bit with her. As I started this book I immediately thought “this book will be perfect for her – it’s the same type of thing”!<br/><br/>So, if you like those shows, books like those shows, books those shows are based on, etc., then this is the book for you. While not the most complex mystery I have read, it is quite a bit </span>
  <span id="freeText18298689304824719831" style="display:none">4 to 4.5 Stars<br /><br />Every time I walk into the living room my wife is watching Pretty Little Liars or Revenge or Riverdale or Veronica Mars or . . . well, you get the idea. Sometimes I watch a bit with her. As I started this book I immediately thought “this book will be perfect for her – it’s the same type of thing”!<br /><br />So, if you like those shows, books like those shows, books those shows are based on, etc., then this is the book for you. While not the most complex mystery I have read, it is quite a bit of fun. Backstabbing rumors, questionable relationships, online gossip all combine to keep you engaged from page one to the Epilogue. There are no lulls or filler here!<br /><br />I voted on this book for the 2017 Goodreads Choice Awards while I was reading it (yeah, that’s right, I wasn’t done with it yet when I voted! Whatcha gonna do about it!? 😁). I stand by my vote – this is a pretty good selection for Young Adult Fiction. If you are a fan of that category, I don’t think you can go wrong. That is, unless you don’t like gossipy cat fights and brooding bad boys in love with nerdy girls . . . hey, if you don’t like those things, why are you even reading the review of a Young Adult book!?!?</span>

<div id="review_2176920713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176920713" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176920713?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141375632" href="/book/show/32887579-one-of-us-is-lying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=illness-mental-terminal">illness-mental-terminal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=sisters">sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176920713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15553243836045312837"><i> ‘Everybody’s got secrets,’ he says. ‘Right?’ </i> <br/><br/>THIS BOOK!! You guys, I thought this book was brilliant! So many great elements all thrown together. <br/><br/>- murder mystery<br/>- high school drama<br/>- secrets, both big and small<br/>- suspicion <br/><br/>I love a murder mystery anyway, but this one was made better as I cared about the 4 kids who were suspects. <br/><br/>The star of the baseball team harbouring a huge secret. <br/>The Prom Queen who has never been able to find herself as a separate person from her long term boyfriend. <br/>The re</span>
  <span id="freeText15553243836045312837" style="display:none"><i> ‘Everybody’s got secrets,’ he says. ‘Right?’ </i> <br /><br />THIS BOOK!! You guys, I thought this book was brilliant! So many great elements all thrown together. <br /><br />- murder mystery<br />- high school drama<br />- secrets, both big and small<br />- suspicion <br /><br />I love a murder mystery anyway, but this one was made better as I cared about the 4 kids who were suspects. <br /><br />The star of the baseball team harbouring a huge secret. <br />The Prom Queen who has never been able to find herself as a separate person from her long term boyfriend. <br />The rebel with previous criminal convictions - the obvious suspect. <br />The goodie two shoes. Surely she’s never broken the rules? <br /><br />All 4 end up in detention with Simon Kelleher, the guy who runs a gossip app that ruins reputations with its secrets. All four of them have a secret to hide and would do anything to keep it hidden. But at what cost? Because by the end of detention Simon is dead, but who did it? <br /><br /><i> ‘Some people are just too toxic to live.’ </i> <br /><br />I was absolutely addicted. I couldn’t put it down until I found out the answer. Plus there are so many tropes that get walked all over. My personal favourite THE GIRL WITH GLASSES GETS THE HOT GUY! This literally never happens in books or films so thank you Karen McManus for including this and not making her take them off ‘to be prettier’<br /><br />I loved Addy’s character development too. In the beginning she was just some jock’s girlfriend with no thoughts of her own. By the end of the book she really became her own person and I LOVED THAT. <br /><br />5 stars ⭐️ for amazing characters, gripping writing, and a killer ending (see what I did there 😉) highly recommend!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15553243836045312837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2176920713">

<div id="review_1978851295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1978851295" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1978851295?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1978851295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11209875508384397696">I feel like one of maybe four people in the world who just... really did not enjoy this book? I've been putting off this review for weeks because I just don't know where to start. I have so many friends who raved about this book to me, so I was <i>so</i> disappointed by it. <br/><br/><b>These are only my opinions, and I would never dream of disrespecting anyone who disagrees with my review, so please show the same courtesy and don't hate me for what I'm about to say. ❤</b><br/><br/><blockquote>→ <b><i>what i liked</i></b> ←</blockquote><br/>This is a very <b>quick</b> read; if I</span>
  <span id="freeText11209875508384397696" style="display:none">I feel like one of maybe four people in the world who just... really did not enjoy this book? I've been putting off this review for weeks because I just don't know where to start. I have so many friends who raved about this book to me, so I was <i>so</i> disappointed by it. <br /><br /><b>These are only my opinions, and I would never dream of disrespecting anyone who disagrees with my review, so please show the same courtesy and don't hate me for what I'm about to say. ❤</b><br /><br /><blockquote>→ <b><i>what i liked</i></b> ←</blockquote><br />This is a very <b>quick</b> read; if I had enjoyed it, I'm sure I would've knocked it out in one sitting. As it was, it still felt like it moved pretty quickly. <br /><br />The <b>main romance</b> is fairly cute. Incredibly trope-y "goody-two-shoes smart girl falls for the brooding bad boy!" stuff, but, I mean, their interactions are fine, and I was rooting for them by the end of the book, which is a big plus. I would say I was more attached to the budding relationship between them than I was to any of the individual characters in this story.<br /><br /><b>Nate, 'the criminal',</b> is a very likable character. He's got a really dark and twisty back story that explains away a lot of his motives, and I definitely enjoyed his perspectives of the story the most. He just feels like a really authentic teen who's trying to muddle through a hard, screwed-up life, and I loved that about him. Whenever it was any other character's POV, I definitely found myself rushing to get back to his sections.<br /><br /><blockquote>→ <b><i>what i didn't like</i></b> ←</blockquote><br />This book is so <b>problematic</b> and most of it is NEVER challenged. First of all, can we talk about the immense amounts of <b>slut-shaming?</b> I could handle it if it was coming just from the characters and/or was actually being challenged consistently, but 1) it isn't challenged every time in the dialogue, and 2) <b>the author contributes to the slut-shaming narrative regarding women cheating.</b><br /><br />We have two characters in the story who are cheaters; one is a female character, who does it one time, while drunk; the other is a male character, who carries on an emotional and physical affair for MONTHS. We spend a tremendous portion of the book focusing on the girl's one-night-stand, while the text literally does not <b>ONCE</b> actually name the boy for what he is: <b>a cheater.</b> There's no remorse shown, and there are no consequences whatsoever for him. It also seems kinda gross to me that the girl who's guilty of cheating is a "pretty, vapid, popular girl" type - can we please stop with these cliches?<br /><br />Also, can we please <b>NOT</b> make the only queer character in the cast a horrible character who cheats and hurts people? AND can we not make the character's coming-out scene a bigger twist than the <i>actual murderer reveal?</i> This book also does some serious vilifying of mental illness, but I won't get started on that rant.<br /><br />Beyond all of that... honestly, the writing is just not that good, and the "twist" is so predictable it hurts.<br /><br /><blockquote>→ <b><i>final thoughts</i></b> ←</blockquote><br />All in all... I almost hated this book. If it hadn't been for the quick pace and how much I enjoyed Nate, as well as his relationship with Bronwyn, I absolutely would have DNFed this. As it stands, I cannot in good conscience recommend this book, and I will <i>probably</i> not be picking up any future releases from this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11209875508384397696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2062113505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2062113505" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2062113505?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062113505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer366920623327672484"><i>”Six hours and five minutes from then we were heading to detention. An hour later, he died.<br/>Seventeen years, gone just like that.”</i><br/><br/>Six people <br/>A detention room<br/>A cup of water<br/>1 teacher<br/><s>5 students</s><br/>4 students<br/>1 dead body<br/><br/>This is the recipe this book was made of and since I enjoyed solving the murder mystery I decided that I won’t go into detail all too much. <br/>This is the kind of book in which you get four POVs and have as much information as the characters that talk about the happenings. You have to guess w</span>
  <span id="freeText366920623327672484" style="display:none"><i>”Six hours and five minutes from then we were heading to detention. An hour later, he died.<br />Seventeen years, gone just like that.”</i><br /><br />Six people <br />A detention room<br />A cup of water<br />1 teacher<br /><s>5 students</s><br />4 students<br />1 dead body<br /><br />This is the recipe this book was made of and since I enjoyed solving the murder mystery I decided that I won’t go into detail all too much. <br />This is the kind of book in which you get four POVs and have as much information as the characters that talk about the happenings. You have to guess with them, you have to experience what they see and you have to take all the pieces of their puzzle and try to solve it. ;-)<br />So who’s the culprit? Whodunnit? <br /><br /><b>Cooper Clay:</b><br /><br />Athlete, Mr. Clean, honourable and honest soul, rising star, likable guy<br />BUT one hell of a secret that might eventually break his neck<br /><br /><b>Nate Macauley:</b><br /><br />Outsider, Drug dealer, black sheep, intelligent loner, on probation, sexy bad boy<br />The obvious culprit, right? ;-P <br /><br /><b>Adelaide Prentiss:</b><br /><br />Yes person, follower, submissive, one of the “cool kids”<br />BUT there’s a fire within her and it’s about to break out<br /><br /><b>Bronwyn Rojas:</b><br /><br />Geek, nice girl, respectable, compassionate and driven<br />Smart enough to plan the perfect murder? <br /><br />Every one of them has a secret, <br />all of them would have had a reason to silence Simon.<br />Yet, nothing ever is what it seems to be. <br /><br />All I’m saying is: <br />Enjoy the ride and have fun guessing! ;-P<br />__________________<br /><br />I wanted to read this book for ages so I was very glad when I went for my <a href="https://thesassylibraryfox.wordpress.com/2019/04/10/hugsnkisses-or-dismissed-by-the-missus-messrs-3/" rel="nofollow noopener">monthly blog meme</a> and chose to “hug and read” it! <br /><br />I really dunno how long <b>“One of Us is Lying”</b> was already on my list but it feels like it’s been on my TBR forever. *lol* <br />To be honest, I don’t even have a clue what it is about. I only know there’s supposed to be a murder and some sort of “Breakfast Club”? XD<br />It sounds promising enough though, so wish me luck! ;-P</span>

  <span id="freeText6976512355853073019" style="display:none">Five kids, one room, one mysterious death, endless possibilities. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533926465ra/26107027.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Locked-Room Mysteries are hands down one of my <b>favorite Mystery subgenres</b>. <br><br>We're talking next level obsessed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557246558ra/27470425.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>They're so nostalgic for me, bringing back memories of family games of Clue, watching <i>Murder, She Wrote</i> with my Mom and binge reading Agatha Christie books whilst on summer vacation. <br><br>Add in the fact that this cast is similar to the stereotypical cast of characters found in <i>The Breakfast Club</i>, one of the best movies EVER created, and you have an equation for a near perfect book for Megs!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549292455ra/27013542.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I listened to the audiobook and was pleased that it had different narrators for each of the main characters. <br><br>They did a fantastic job bringing the story to life and consequently, I flew through it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488657610ra/22141392.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though I predicted the <i>whodunit</i> less than halfway through, I still ended up genuinely enjoying the story. <br><br>Getting to the conclusion was pure fun and I never felt bored, or that the story was dragging.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513155554ra/24666756.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Each chapter is told from the perspective of one of the suspects, one of the four kids left alive after detention, and each chapter ended in a revelation of incriminating facts related to that character. I felt that format really pushed the narrative along at a nice, steady pace.<br><br>This was my first Karen M. McManus book and I look forward to picking up more books from her in the future!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1598836705ra/30038448.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2065648304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2065648304" />
    <a title="Annemarie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie"><img alt="Annemarie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593255949p2/27544490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065648304?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annemarie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annemarie" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie">Annemarie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783570165126" href="/book/show/36978038-one-of-us-is-lying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=read-in-german">read-in-german</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065648304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10796773229390542405">As a huge fan of "The Breakfast Club", I loved the concept of five characters with different personalities meeting in detention from the get go, and I'm incredibly happy to report that my high expectations were even exceeded! <br/>(By the way, besides the detention-concept, the story is completely different from "The Breakfast Club", so you don't need to fear that this is some cheap knockoff!)<br/><br/>All the main characters get introduced within a few pages right at the beginning. I often find this rather pr</span>
  <span id="freeText10796773229390542405" style="display:none">As a huge fan of "The Breakfast Club", I loved the concept of five characters with different personalities meeting in detention from the get go, and I'm incredibly happy to report that my high expectations were even exceeded! <br />(By the way, besides the detention-concept, the story is completely different from "The Breakfast Club", so you don't need to fear that this is some cheap knockoff!)<br /><br />All the main characters get introduced within a few pages right at the beginning. I often find this rather problematic, as I easily get confused by many characters entering the scene at once, and I then have trouble telling them apart. This was not the case here! I surprisingly was able to tell them apart easily and developed a picture of them in my head right away. <br /><br />I fell in love with all of them and their different personalities. Besides the main plot, everyone has a personal and interesting storyline as well. They all live/lived through some not so nice things, but none of them play the victim. They have realistic views on their situations and aren't delusional. I was so happy about that! It often ticks me off when I see teenagers acting like little children in YA-novels, so it was nice to see something else for once.<br /><br />Actually, there were many opportunities to go down the typical YA-route, but thankfully that didn't happen. I was very (pleasantly) surprised at that! <br />Sure, there were some (very) minimal cheesy scenes, but I (unexpectedly) found them rather cute, and not annoying and unnecessary like I usually do. There are also kept on a small scale, so the attention never drifts away from the main plot.<br /><br />All of the characters go through some personal growth throughout the book. This growth is done realistically; nothing is over the top or too unbelievable. <br />My personal favorite was Addy - I truly had a soft spot for her! Her individual storyline and development is something so important. I was rooting for her the whole way through and was cheering her on at every step of the way. I'm sure that they are people reading this book who are in the same situation as her, and I really, really hope that their eyes might be opened with the help of Addy's portrayal.<br /><br />The title obviously keeps you guessing throughout. The level of suspense was perfect and I never knew who and what to trust and believe. I kept thinking about possible solutions even when I wasn't reading. I thought I had discovered every possible solution, but I was still surprised at the end!<br /><br />There is only one small thing I have to complain about: I would have liked a little bit more insight into Simon's life. But to be honest, I'm not even too bothered about this though, as all the fantastic things definitely outweigh this small issue.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10796773229390542405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303899227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10265895437181356458">It sounds like the Breakfast Club with five teenagers, all from different groups, stuck together in detention. Yet things are off from the start, all of the kids claim that the cellphones that landed them there didn't belong to them. When one of them suddenly collapses from an anaphylactic attack, things get even stranger. Now Simon, the boy who had that anaphylactic attack, is dead and everyone in the room is a suspect when the tox screen comes back and it becomes clear that someone purposefull</span>
  <span id="freeText10265895437181356458" style="display:none">It sounds like the Breakfast Club with five teenagers, all from different groups, stuck together in detention. Yet things are off from the start, all of the kids claim that the cellphones that landed them there didn't belong to them. When one of them suddenly collapses from an anaphylactic attack, things get even stranger. Now Simon, the boy who had that anaphylactic attack, is dead and everyone in the room is a suspect when the tox screen comes back and it becomes clear that someone purposefully gave him peanut oil. <br /><br />Uh spoilers probably?? ok most likely I can't really shut up so. Anyway I really enjoyed this one. It reminded me of one of those CW shows, and like I've said before, that is something I'm totally into. I just totally felt like a teenager again while reading this, in a good way, and that was fun. I even liked the ending here and I'm usually pretty eh about endings most of the time. It was a happy ending but it also felt real enough that I wasn't vomiting from how amazing everything was. I can't stand saccharine sweet endings. I mean I wish Nick hadn't pushed Bronwyn away after he gets out of jail but it felt like a really consistent reaction when considering the rest of his behavior in the book. <br /><br />Also I really liked how each character's POV felt like an individual new person. I think a lot of times when authors have multiple POVs it feels like all the voices sort of blend together and sound too similar. And can I just say I really lobed Addy's growth as a character, like yes fuck your dick head boyfriend. Speaking of which the whole Jake thing was pretty fucked up. Once they started talking about Simon posting on 4chan on school shooting threads, I knew he set it up, but I totally didn't see the Jake thing coming. I also don't even know what to say about that because like what a huge fucking overreaction honestly, like just cause your girlfriend cheats on you doesn't mean you let someone who was your friend kill themselves and then frame her for it jesus fucking christ. <br /><br />I also saw a bunch of reviews about the portrayal about sexuality and mental illness, and I'm not trying to disqualify anyone else's opinions or feelings but personally I didn't find it consistent with my own reading of the book. I don't think the author ever really slut shames, like the villain is the one doing it and it's clearly not endorsed. Also the homophobia wasn't glorified either. The picture of mental illness it paints isnt that nuanced but this book reads like pretty little liars or something and I wasn't really expecting it to have some conversation inducing portrayals of those things. It plays up on the drama and stereotypes and I guess thats not enjoyable for everyone but I personally liked it and just read for the enjoyment aspect more than much else. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10265895437181356458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2000180114" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000180114" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2000180114?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2000180114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13388719831146302786">This is an <i>adequate</i> mystery YA novel. The writing is engaging and accessible. The story itself is narrated by the four main characters—Bronwyn, Addy, Nate and Cooper—, thus keeping things moving at a fast pace. <br/><br/>I was very curious about this book. How can one not be, when hearing the premise? Five students walk into the detention room and only four come out? I love these kinds of stories—like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16299.And_Then_There_Were_None' title='And Then There Were None by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>And Then There Were None</a>—in which everyone is a suspect and no one is to be trusted. <br/><br/>But I was disappoint</span>
  <span id="freeText13388719831146302786" style="display:none">This is an <i>adequate</i> mystery YA novel. The writing is engaging and accessible. The story itself is narrated by the four main characters—Bronwyn, Addy, Nate and Cooper—, thus keeping things moving at a fast pace. <br /><br />I was very curious about this book. How can one not be, when hearing the premise? Five students walk into the detention room and only four come out? I love these kinds of stories—like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16299.And_Then_There_Were_None" title="And Then There Were None by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">And Then There Were None</a>—in which everyone is a suspect and no one is to be trusted. <br /><br />But I was disappointed with the story. I never felt thrilled and I never felt mystified. That’s the problem: this book doesn’t make you feel <i>anything</i>. And the way I see it, it’s a requirement for mysteries/thrillers to make you feel <i>something</i>. Otherwise it’s just a book like any other. You could say that I wasn't as invested in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395.One_of_Us_Is_Lying" title="One of Us Is Lying by Karen M. McManus" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us Is Lying</a> as I would have wanted to be.<br /><br />I liked how different the characters were from one another, even if they are complete clichés. The synopsis makes that perfectly clear from the start. However, as the story progresses, we discover new facets of their personalities. I cared for the future of each of them, but I wouldn’t go as far as to say that I’ve never met anyone like Bronwyn, Addy, Nate or Cooper. Because again, clichés. <br /><br />If this is one of the first YA mystery novels that you read, I guess there’s a chance you’ll enjoy it more than I did. Honestly I just can’t stop thinking of better YA mystery novels than this one. But that’s because I’ve read many of them.<br /><br />Here are some recommendations:<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16074758.Dangerous_Girls" title="Dangerous Girls by Abigail Haas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Girls</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24382227.Dreamland_Burning" title="Dreamland Burning by Jennifer Latham" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreamland Burning</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21853636.All_the_Rage" title="All the Rage by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Rage</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33956433.City_of_Saints___Thieves" title="City of Saints &amp; Thieves by Natalie C. Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Saints &amp; Thieves</a><br /><br />Those are books that actually make you feel something.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13388719831146302786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12157888836450687987" style="display:none">This book should be called All of Us Are Liars.<br /><br />One of Us Is Lying was fasted paced, fun, and very addictive. Once I picked this book up I could not put it down. It also served as a pallet cleanser after The Handmaid's Tale. I needed something fun and lighter in tone(yes I know its about the murder of a teenager). <br /><br />At about 100 pages in I developed a theory about who was behind the crime and it turns out I was right. All my years of watching SVU, Criminal Minds, and 48 Hours have not been in vain. I should probably quit the Library and become a PI or Bounty Hunter, I'd be amazing at it. <br /><br />One of Us Is Lying is Karen McManus' debut novel and I can't wait to read more of her work in the future. <div id="review_2018773223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2018773223" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2018773223?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2018773223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12164060249916481658">Is this what <i>AKLDSBSAJL;FRSFWHATTHEFUCKJUSTHAPPENED???</i> feels like? Because I think I just experienced that shit, dude. <br/><br/>My heart is literally beating so fast from this thrill and mystery and feels fulfilled with something heavy called <i>satisfaction</i>. I haven't been so content and had screamy feels over a thriller since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16074758.Dangerous_Girls' title='Dangerous Girls by Abigail Haas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dangerous Girls</a>, which was 213324 decades ago. <br/><br/>Tbh, it's so hard to find a thriller that literally has you on the edge of your seat, biting your nails, screaming at and suspecting ev</span>
  <span id="freeText12164060249916481658" style="display:none">Is this what <i>AKLDSBSAJL;FRSFWHATTHEFUCKJUSTHAPPENED???</i> feels like? Because I think I just experienced that shit, dude. <br><br>My heart is literally beating so fast from this thrill and mystery and feels fulfilled with something heavy called <i>satisfaction</i>. I haven't been so content and had screamy feels over a thriller since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16074758.Dangerous_Girls" title="Dangerous Girls by Abigail Haas" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Girls</a>, which was 213324 decades ago. <br><br>Tbh, it's so hard to find a thriller that literally has you on the edge of your seat, biting your nails, screaming at and suspecting everyone, saying "WHAT THE FUCK" every 3 pages, wanting to flip to the last page to find out who dunnit because you're so fucking full of it and can't stand the mystery and suspense. <br><br>It's so hard to find a thriller that's actually???? <i>thrilling???</i><br><br>Well, I can 99% gaurentee your search has come to the end because let me present to you <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395-one-of-us-is-lying" rel="nofollow noopener">this book</a> </i>which lives up to the damn hype and everything you can possibly want in a thriller. <br><br><u>What it's about:</u><br>You, you're a murder suspect and all your secrets are gonna be exposed, have a nicE LIFE!!! Want a cookie? :))<br><br>Ight, seriously, these 5 kids get in trouble and have detention where they're talking and it's all detention stuff when one of the kids starts choking and having an allergic reaction. he's taken to the hospital and later the four kids find out he dies. His death is all suspicious and now all four of 'em are suspects and we need to figure who dunnit and who's lying. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“She's a princess and you're a jock," he says. He thrusts his chin toward Bronwyn, then at Nate. "And you're a brain. And you're a criminal. You're all walking teen-movie stereotypes.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Addy, Nate, Cooper and Bronwyn are incredible characters, imo. After being put under suspicion, the four of these learn so much about themselves and make decisions that is best for themselves and for everyone. It's heartbreaking and sad to learn about what they hide, but spoilers so read it and find out yourself, thanks. :)<br><br>No but seriously, these are the type of characters, I wouldn't associate with at all when first reading about them, but like???? honestly, I'm willing to turn myself in if it means having them free and unharmed. i love them so much oh my god. <br><br>Can we talk about how precious Cooper is? This kid, without a doubt, is my favorite. i love this precious cinnamon roll so much. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421353201ra/13364472.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>^yes bro, this is an actual footage of me caught hugging Cooper, bYE.<br><br>Also, I guessed it oh my god. I think it's because I'm so obsessed with non fiction crime and murder or probably because I'm just plain morbid??? But even though I had my predictions, I was <i>shook</i> when that ending happened, son.<br><br>Overall, this book is so fucking precious and I totally recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12164060249916481658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897061694" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897061694?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34931507-one-of-us-is-lying">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=thriven-thrillers">thriven-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=contemporary-cuteness">contemporary-cuteness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=mysterious-miasmas">mysterious-miasmas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897061694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7438649192920440906"><b>First Read: April 2017, Rating: 4 stars<br/>Second Read: November 2020, Rating: 4 stars</b><br/><br/>After a typical day in a typical American high school, five teenagers enter detention but only four make it out alive. Simon, notorious due to his gossip-style blog that revealed all the dark and dirty secrets his fellow students never thought would see the light of day, had made many enemies. But which one would want to see him dead? Which one of them is lying?<br/><br/>The multiple perspectives all provided their own angle</span>
  <span id="freeText7438649192920440906" style="display:none"><b>First Read: April 2017, Rating: 4 stars<br />Second Read: November 2020, Rating: 4 stars</b><br /><br />After a typical day in a typical American high school, five teenagers enter detention but only four make it out alive. Simon, notorious due to his gossip-style blog that revealed all the dark and dirty secrets his fellow students never thought would see the light of day, had made many enemies. But which one would want to see him dead? Which one of them is lying?<br /><br />The multiple perspectives all provided their own angle to the plot. These all pulled together, towards the end, to turn their individual stories into one cohesive whole. Each dirty secret that was uncovered made each character less of a walking stereotype and more of a flawed, and therefore real, individual. I will admit that when I first was introduced to this cast of characters - the overachiever, the bad boy, the jock, and the popular girl - I had assumed these were going to be nothing more than a set of weakly constructed and overused cardboard characters. How wrong could I be?<br /><br />The actual plot was a thrilling and interesting one, but it was the characters who circled it that really compelled me to keep reading. I admit that I figured out part of the mystery pretty quickly, but this didn't detract from my enjoyment in any way, purely because the characters. With their flaws and their individual insights they continued to interest me, and made this a very real and very suspenseful read.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to the author, Karen M. McManus, and the publisher, Delacorte Press, for this opportunity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7438649192920440906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10403623321452929096" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“Some people are too toxic to live. They just are.”</i>
</b><br><br>Welcome to detention, where a princess, a jock, a brain, a criminal and . . . a gossip???? Wait, that’s not historically accurate . . . . .<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487786334ra/22051185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Have all earned a spot for violating one of the most serious rules of high school: NO PHONES IN CLASS. They’ve done the crime, now they have to do the time as well as write a 500 word essay about how technology is ruining American high schools. If they fail to do so, well . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Plans quickly change, however, when the gossip drops dead of anaphylactic shock. (He didn’t belong in the story anyway, right? The basketcase was the final member.) Now the four remaining delinquents are all suspects in his death when the questions of just how did peanut oil get in the disposable cups near the sink and what happened to all of the epi pens in the nurse’s station get raised. But there’s even more in store for these kids when the gossip’s dishy blog starts revealing secrets none of the four ever thought would get out . . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
